ns-0 ns-subject mw-editable page-Kinetic_theory_of_gases rootpage-Kinetic_theory_of_gases skin-vector action-view"> <div class="noprint" id="mw-page-base"></div>\n<div class="noprint" id="mw-head-base"></div>\n<div class="mw-body" id="content" role="main">\n<a id="top"></a>\n<div class="mw-body-content" id="siteNotice"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Kinetic theory of gases</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Translational_motion.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Translational_motion.gif" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Translational_motion.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> of an ideal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monatomic" title="Monatomic">monatomic</a> <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a> is proportional to the average <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> of its atoms. The <a href="/wiki/Bohr_radius" title="Bohr radius">size</a> of <a href="/wiki/Helium" title="Helium">helium</a> atoms relative to their spacing is shown to scale under 1950 <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_(unit)" title="Atmosphere (unit)">atmospheres</a> of pressure. The atoms have a certain, average speed, slowed down here two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1000000000000_(number)" title="1000000000000 (number)">trillion</a> fold from room temperature.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>kinetic theory of gases</b> describes a <a href="/wiki/Gas" title="Gas">gas</a> as a large number of submicroscopic <a href="/wiki/Particle" title="Particle">particles</a> (<a href="/wiki/Atom" title="Atom">atoms</a> or <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">molecules</a>), all of which are in constant, rapid, <a href="/wiki/Randomness" title="Randomness">random</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_(physics)" title="Motion (physics)">motion</a>. The randomness arises from the particles\' many collisions with each other and with the walls of the container.\n</p><p>Kinetic theory of gases explains the <a href="/wiki/Macroscopic_scale" title="Macroscopic scale">macroscopic</a> properties of gases, such as pressure, temperature, viscosity, <a href="/wiki/Thermal_conductivity" title="Thermal conductivity">thermal conductivity</a>, and volume, by considering their molecular composition and motion. The theory posits that gas pressure results from particles\' collisions with the walls of a container at different velocities.\n</p><p>Kinetic molecular theory defines temperature in its own way, in contrast with the <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">thermodynamic definition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C_&amp;_C_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-C_&amp;_C-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under an <a href="/wiki/Optical_microscope" title="Optical microscope">optical microscope</a>, the molecules making up a liquid are too small to be visible. However, the jittery motion of pollen grains or dust particles in liquid are visible. Known as <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, the motion of the pollen or dust results from their collisions with the liquid\'s molecules.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Assumptions"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Assumptions</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Equilibrium_properties"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Equilibrium properties</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Pressure_and_kinetic_energy"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Pressure and kinetic energy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Temperature_and_kinetic_energy"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Temperature and kinetic energy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#Collisions_with_container"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Collisions with container</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7"><a href="#Speed_of_molecules"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Speed of molecules</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Transport_properties"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Transport properties</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Diffusion_Coefficient_and_diffusion_flux"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Diffusion Coefficient and diffusion flux</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Viscosity_and_kinetic_momentum"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Viscosity and kinetic momentum</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Thermal_conductivity_and_heat_flux"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Thermal conductivity and heat flux</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In approximately 50 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Before_common_era" title="Before common era">BCE</a>, the Roman philosopher <a href="/wiki/Lucretius" title="Lucretius">Lucretius</a> proposed that apparently static macroscopic bodies were composed on a small scale of rapidly moving atoms all bouncing off each other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Epicureanism" title="Epicureanism">Epicurean</a> atomistic point of view was rarely considered in the subsequent centuries, when <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotlean</a> ideas were dominant.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HYDRODYNAMICA,_Danielis_Bernoulli.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1214" data-file-width="883" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png/170px-HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png/255px-HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png/340px-HYDRODYNAMICA%2C_Danielis_Bernoulli.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HYDRODYNAMICA,_Danielis_Bernoulli.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hydrodynamica front cover</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1738 <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bernoulli" title="Daniel Bernoulli">Daniel Bernoulli</a> published <i><a href="/wiki/Hydrodynamica" title="Hydrodynamica">Hydrodynamica</a></i>, which laid the basis for the kinetic theory of gases.  In this work, Bernoulli posited the argument, still used to this day, that gases consist of great numbers of molecules moving in all directions, that their impact on a surface causes the gas pressure that we feel, and that what we experience as <a href="/wiki/Heat" title="Heat">heat</a> is simply the <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> of their motion. The theory was not immediately accepted, in part because <a href="/wiki/Conservation_of_energy" title="Conservation of energy">conservation of energy</a> had not yet been established, and it was not obvious to physicists how the collisions between molecules could be perfectly elastic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PonomarevKurchatov1993_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-PonomarevKurchatov1993-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>36&#8211;37</span></sup>\n</p><p>Other pioneers of the kinetic theory (which were neglected by their contemporaries) were <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> (1747),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georges-Louis_Le_Sage" title="Georges-Louis Le Sage">Georges-Louis Le Sage</a> (ca. 1780, published 1818),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Herapath" title="John Herapath">John Herapath</a> (1816)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_James_Waterston" title="John James Waterston">John James Waterston</a> (1843),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> which connected their research with the development of <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_explanations_of_gravitation" title="Mechanical explanations of gravitation">mechanical explanations of gravitation</a>. In 1856 <a href="/wiki/August_Kr%C3%B6nig" title="August Kr&#246;nig">August Kr&#246;nig</a> (probably after reading a paper of Waterston) created a simple gas-kinetic model, which only considered the translational motion of the particles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1857 <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Clausius" title="Rudolf Clausius">Rudolf Clausius</a>, according to his own words independently of Kr&#246;nig, developed a similar, but much more sophisticated version of the theory which included translational and contrary to Kr&#246;nig also rotational and vibrational molecular motions. In this same work he introduced the concept of <a href="/wiki/Mean_free_path" title="Mean free path">mean free path</a> of a particle.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In 1859, after reading a paper on the diffusion of molecules by <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Clausius" title="Rudolf Clausius">Rudolf Clausius</a>, Scottish physicist <a href="/wiki/James_Clerk_Maxwell" title="James Clerk Maxwell">James Clerk Maxwell</a> formulated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maxwell_distribution" title="Maxwell distribution">Maxwell distribution</a> of molecular velocities, which gave the proportion of molecules having a certain velocity in a specific range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> This was the first-ever statistical law in physics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Maxwell also gave the first mechanical argument that molecular collisions entail an equalization of temperatures and hence a tendency towards equilibrium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> In his 1873 thirteen page article \'Molecules\', Maxwell states: "we are told that an \'atom\' is a material point, invested and surrounded by \'potential forces\' and that when \'flying molecules\' strike against a solid body in constant succession it causes what is called <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">pressure</a> of air and other gases."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\nIn 1871, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Boltzmann" title="Ludwig Boltzmann">Ludwig Boltzmann</a> generalized Maxwell\'s achievement and formulated the <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%E2%80%93Boltzmann_distribution" title="Maxwell&#8211;Boltzmann distribution">Maxwell&#8211;Boltzmann distribution</a>. Also the <a href="/wiki/Logarithm" title="Logarithm">logarithmic</a> connection between <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">entropy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Probability" title="Probability">probability</a> was first stated by him.\n</p><p>In the beginning of the twentieth century, however, atoms were considered by many physicists to be purely hypothetical constructs, rather than real objects. An important turning point was <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>\'s (1905)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Marian_Smoluchowski" title="Marian Smoluchowski">Marian Smoluchowski</a>\'s (1906)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>\npapers on <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">Brownian motion</a>, which succeeded in making certain accurate quantitative predictions based on the kinetic theory.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assumptions">Assumptions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Assumptions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The theory for ideal gases makes the following assumptions:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The gas consists of very small particles known as molecules. This smallness of their size is such that the total <a href="/wiki/Volume" title="Volume">volume</a> of the individual gas molecules added up is negligible compared to the volume of the smallest open ball containing all the molecules. This is equivalent to stating that the average distance separating the gas particles is large compared to their <a href="/wiki/Atomic_radius" title="Atomic radius">size</a>.</li>\n<li>These particles have the same <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a>.</li>\n<li>The number of molecules is so large that statistical treatment can be applied.</li></ul>\n<ul><li>The rapidly moving particles constantly collide among themselves and with the walls of the container. All these collisions are perfectly elastic. This means the molecules are considered to be perfectly spherical in shape and elastic in nature.</li>\n<li>Except during collisions, the <a href="/wiki/Interaction" title="Interaction">interactions</a> among molecules are negligible. (That is, they exert no <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">forces</a> on one another.)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd>This implies:\n<dl><dd>1. <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">Relativistic</a> effects are negligible.</dd>\n<dd>2. <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">Quantum-mechanical</a> effects are negligible. This means that the <a href="/wiki/Mean_inter-particle_distance" title="Mean inter-particle distance">inter-particle distance</a> is much larger than the <a href="/wiki/Thermal_de_Broglie_wavelength" title="Thermal de Broglie wavelength">thermal de Broglie wavelength</a> and the molecules are treated as <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical</a> <a href="/wiki/Physical_body" title="Physical body">objects</a>.</dd>\n<dd>3. Because of the above two, their dynamics can be treated classically. This means that the equations of motion of the molecules are time-reversible.</dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<ul><li>The average kinetic energy of the gas particles depends only on the <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_temperature" title="Thermodynamic temperature">absolute temperature</a> of the <a href="/wiki/System" title="System">system</a>. The kinetic theory has its own definition of temperature, not identical with the thermodynamic definition.</li>\n<li>The elapsed time of a collision between a molecule and the container\'s wall is negligible when compared to the time between successive collisions.</li>\n<li>There are negligible gravitational force on molecules.</li></ul>\n<p>More modern developments relax these assumptions and are based on the <a href="/wiki/Boltzmann_equation" title="Boltzmann equation">Boltzmann equation</a>. These can accurately describe the properties of dense gases, because they include the volume of the molecules. The necessary assumptions are the absence of quantum effects, <a href="/wiki/Molecular_chaos" title="Molecular chaos">molecular chaos</a> and small gradients in bulk properties. Expansions to higher orders in the density are known as <a href="/wiki/Virial_expansion" title="Virial expansion">virial expansions</a>.\n</p><p>An important book on kinetic theory is that by <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Chapman_(mathematician)" title="Sydney Chapman (mathematician)">Chapman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cowling" title="Thomas Cowling">Cowling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-C_&amp;_C_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-C_&amp;_C-1">[1]</a></sup> An important approach to the subject is called <a href="/wiki/Chapman%E2%80%93Enskog_theory" title="Chapman&#8211;Enskog theory">Chapman&#8211;Enskog theory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> There have been many modern developments and there is an alternative approach developed by Grad based on moment expansions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\nIn the other limit, for extremely rarefied gases, the gradients in bulk properties are not small compared to the mean free paths. This is known as the Knudsen regime and expansions can be performed in the <a href="/wiki/Knudsen_number" title="Knudsen number">Knudsen number</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equilibrium_properties">Equilibrium properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Equilibrium properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pressure_and_kinetic_energy"><span id="Pressure_and_Kinetic_Energy"></span>Pressure and kinetic energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pressure and kinetic energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In kinetic model of gases, the <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">pressure</a> is equal to the force exerted by the atoms hitting and rebounding from a unit area of the gas container surface. Consider a gas of <i>N</i> molecules, each of mass <i>m</i>, enclosed in a cube of volume <i>V</i> = <i>L</i><sup>3</sup>. When a gas molecule collides with the wall of the container perpendicular to the <i>x</i> axis and bounces off in the opposite direction with the same speed (an <a href="/wiki/Elastic_collision" title="Elastic collision">elastic collision</a>), the change in <a href="/wiki/Momentum" title="Momentum">momentum</a> is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta p=p_{i,x}-p_{f,x}=p_{i,x}-(-p_{i,x})=2p_{i,x}=2mv_{x},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>f</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<msub>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>i</mi>\n<mo>,</mo>\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<msub>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta p=p_{i,x}-p_{f,x}=p_{i,x}-(-p_{i,x})=2p_{i,x}=2mv_{x},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta p=p_{i,x}-p_{f,x}=p_{i,x}-(-p_{i,x})=2p_{i,x}=2mv_{x},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d07838b76dd4a9ea62ad1cbd52aa5c3c2f0980cc" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:49.28ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>p</i> is the momentum, <i>i</i> and <i>f</i> indicate initial and final momentum (before and after collision), <i>x</i> indicates that only the <i>x</i> direction is being considered, and <i>v</i> is the speed of the <a href="/wiki/Particle" title="Particle">particle</a> (which is the same before and after the collision).\n</p><p>The particle impacts one specific side wall once every\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t={\\frac {2L}{v_{x}}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; --></mi>\n<mi>t</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\Delta t={\\frac {2L}{v_{x}}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta t={\\frac {2L}{v_{x}}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c9387700fb56b70129f25e9179c36679e8534388" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:10.102ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>L</i> is the distance between opposite walls.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">force</a> due to this particle is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F={\\frac {\\Delta p}{\\Delta t}}={\\frac {mv_{x}^{2}}{L}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#916;<!-- &#916; width:17.703ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The total force on the wall is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle F={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v_{x}^{2}}}}{L}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>F</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>x</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<msubsup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>z</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msubsup>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mi>L</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle F={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}}}{3L}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="F={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}}}{3L}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6d7516ebc55f11012c6864bec9c0aa0c338a0393" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; Therefore, the pressure of the gas is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle P={\\frac {F}{L^{2}}}={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}}}{3V}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>F</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>L</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mi>V</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>,</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P={\\frac {F}{L^{2}}}={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}}}{3V}},}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle P={\\frac {F}{L^{2}}}={\\frac {Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}}}{3V}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9c74a6e3a9bfe7b7ddcc2ca072d2c18d81910807" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:19.299ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <i>V</i> = <i>L</i><sup>3</sup> is the volume of the box.\n</p><p>In terms of the kinetic energy of the gas <i>K</i>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle PV={\\frac {2}{3}}\\times {K}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n<mi>V</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#215;<!-- &#215; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>K</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle PV={\\frac {2}{3}}\\times {K}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle PV={\\frac {2}{3}}\\times {K}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9b2ece6a2583f25c7b22788826e7986c95e93ed6" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:14.183ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>This is a first non-trivial result of the kinetic theory because it relates pressure, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macroscopic" title="Macroscopic">macroscopic</a> property, to the  (translational) <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a> of the molecules <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle N{\\frac {1}{2}}m{\\overline {v^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; --></mo>\n</mover>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle N{\\frac {1}{2}}m{\\overline {v^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle N{\\frac {1}{2}}m{\\overline {v^{2}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/977a8485bc68fc2db6c08fc33ba49ffa1b65c7ad" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:8.399ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span>, which is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microscopic" title="Microscopic">microscopic</a> property.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature_and_kinetic_energy">Temperature and kinetic energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Temperature and kinetic energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Rewriting the above result for the pressure as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle PV={Nm{\\overline {v^{2}}} \\over 3}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n<mi>V</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>N</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mover>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo accent="false">&#175;<!-- &#175; background:none; margin:0; border:none;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="nowrap" style="vertical-align:middle; border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0;"><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle PV={\\frac {2}{3}}K.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n<mi>V</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mi>K</mi>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle PV={\\frac {2}{3}}K.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\n   \\displaystyle \n   PV \n   =\n   \\frac\n   {2}\n   {3}\n   K.\n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8ea9f814bf758d3702fae79647d787ef594e9b38" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; margin:0; border:none; width:99%;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td rowspan="2" style="border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0; font-size:4pt;">&#160;</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width:100%; border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0; font-size:1pt;">&#160;</p>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="2" style="border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0; font-size:4pt;">&#160;</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="border-left:none; border-top:0px none #e5e5e5; border-right:none; border-bottom:none; padding:0.08em;">\n<p style="margin:0; font-size:1pt;">&#160;</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n</td>\n<td class="nowrap" style="vertical-align:middle; border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0pt;"><b>(<span class="reference nourlexpansion" id="math_4" style="font-weight:bold; font-style:italic;">4</span>)</b></p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<p>Thus, the product of pressure and\nvolume per <a href="/wiki/Mole_(unit)" title="Mole (unit)">mole</a> is proportional to the average\n(translational) molecular kinetic energy.\n</p><p>Eq.(<b><a href="#math_1">1</a></b>) and Eq.(<b><a href="#math_4">4</a></b>)\nare called the "classical results",\nwhich could also be derived from <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">statistical mechanics</a>;\nfor more details, see:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since there are\n<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle 3N}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle 3N}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\displaystyle 3N" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3aea1927588c3631f9c5f634ca3791337961d5d8" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.226ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>\n<a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_freedom_(physics_and_chemistry)" title="Degrees of freedom (physics and chemistry)">degrees of freedom</a> in a monatomic-gas system with\n<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle N}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle N}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\displaystyle N" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2f40d155d320413e3eb0c76a591f513b2f386c68" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.064ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>\nparticles,\nthe kinetic energy per degree of freedom per molecule is\n</p>\n<dl><dd>\n<table style="border-collapse:collapse; background:none; margin:0; border:none;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="nowrap" style="vertical-align:middle; border:none; padding:0.08em;"><p style="margin:0;"><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle {\\frac {K}{3N}}={\\frac {k_{B}T}{2}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>K</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mn>3</mn>\n<mi>N</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<msub>\n<mi>k</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>B</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mi>T</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\displaystyle {\\frac {K}{3N}}={\\frac {k_{B}T}{2}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\n   \\displaystyle \n   \\frac\n   {K}\n   {3 N}\n   =\n   \\frac\n   {k_B T}\n   {2}\n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ee61a25e142128579b7247488ed21eff5c350037" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; In addition to this, the temperature will decrease when the pressure drops to a certain point.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The reason for this is unclear. (June 2014)">why?</span></a></i>]</sup>\nThis result is related\nto the <a href="/wiki/Equipartition_theorem" title="Equipartition theorem">equipartition theorem</a>.\n</p><p>As noted in the article on <a href="/wiki/Heat_capacity" title="Heat capacity">heat capacity</a>, diatomic\ngases should have 7 degrees of freedom, but the lighter diatomic gases act\nas if they have only 5. Monatomic gases have 3 degrees of freedom.\n</p><p>Thus the kinetic energy per kelvin (monatomic <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">ideal gas</a>) is 3 [R/2] = 3R/2:\n</p>\n<ul><li>per mole: 12.47 J</li>\n<li>per molecule: 20.7 yJ = 129 &#956;eV.</li></ul>\n<p>At <a href="/wiki/Standard_conditions_for_temperature_and_pressure" title="Standard conditions for temperature and pressure">standard temperature</a> (273.15 K), we get:\n</p>\n<ul><li>per mole: 3406 J</li>\n<li>per molecule: 5.65 zJ = 35.2 meV.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collisions_with_container">Collisions with container</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kinetic_theory_of_gases&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Collisions with container">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The total number and velocity distribution of particles hitting the container wall can be calculated<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OCW_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-OCW-20">[20]</a></sup> based on naive kinetic theory, and the result can be used for analyzing <a href="/wiki/Effusion" title="Effusion">effusion into vacuum</a>:\n</p><p>Assume that, in the container, the number density is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\rho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#961;<!-- &#961;
